IN THE CHAIR: ROBERTA METSOLA
President

ГӮВ 
1. Resumption of the session
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ I declare resumed the session of the European Parliament adjourned on 22 May 2025.

ГӮВ 

2. Opening of the sitting
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ ГӮВ 

(The sitting opened at 17:00)

ГӮВ 

3. Statement by the President
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ Dear colleagues, welcome back to Strasbourg for our plenary session. I'll start with a sad communication on what happened in Austria.

Last week, we learned of the horrific school shooting in Graz, where a former pupil killed 10 students and staff, and severely injured many others. This was a senseless act of violence that has deeply shaken Austria and all of Europe. Our thoughts are with the victims, their families and the entire school community. We stand with everyone in Austria at this terrible time.

That same day, we learned of another brutal attack, as a 31-year-old teaching assistant was stabbed to death outside a school in Nogent in France. La victime et ses proches sont dans nos pensГғВ©es.

Violence and hatred, dear colleagues, have no place in Europe and no place in our schools. Schools must remain safe spaces of learning and growth ГўВҖВ“ never of fear. So I ask you to please join me in observing a minute's silence in honour of the victims and all those affected.

(The House rose and observed a minuteГўВҖВҷs silence)

ГӮВ 

4. Approval of the minutes of the previous sittings
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ The minutes and the texts adopted of the sitting of 21 and 22 May 20205 are available.

Are there any comments? No?

The minutes are therefore approved.

ГӮВ

Video of the speeches

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ Following the resignation of OndГ…Вҷej KovaГ…ВҷГғВӯk, and on the proposal of the Committee on Legal Affairs, Parliament takes note of the vacancy of his seat from 31ГӮВ July 2025, in accordance with the Rules of Procedure, and will inform the national authority concerned thereof.

This request is referred to the Committee on Legal Affairs.

ГӮВ

Video of the speeches

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ I have received a letter from the competent authorities in Belgium withdrawing the request for the waiver of the parliamentary immunity of our colleague Giusi Princi. The procedure is therefore closed.

ГӮВ 

8. Requests for the defence of the immunity of a former Member ГўВҖВ“ termination of procedure
Video of the speeches

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ The Committee on Legal Affairs has informed me that the request for defence of the parliamentary immunity of Helmut GeukingГӮВ is inadmissible, so the procedure is therefore closed.

ГӮВ 

11. Interpretation of the Rules of Procedure
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ The AFCO Committee has proposed interpretations of the first subparagraph of ArticleГӮВ 3(5)ГӮВ and ArticleГӮВ 8 of Annex I to Parliament's Rules of Procedure. The texts are available on the plenary webpage and will be published in the minutes of the sitting.

Pursuant to Rule 242(4), Members or a political group reaching at least the low threshold may contest the committee's interpretations within a period of 24ГӮВ hours following this announcement. If the interpretations are not contested, they shall be deemed approved.

ГӮВ 

12. Negotiations ahead of ParliamentГўВҖВҷs first reading (Rule 72)
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ The LIBE Committee has decided to enter interinstitutional negotiations, pursuant to RuleГӮВ 72(1) of the Rules of Procedure. The report which constitutes the mandate for the negotiations is available on the plenary webpage and the title will be published in the minutes of the sitting.

Pursuant to Rule 72(2), Members or political groups reaching at least the medium threshold may request in writing by midnight tomorrow, Tuesday, 17ГӮВ June, that the decision be put to the vote. If no request for a vote in Parliament is made within the deadline, the committee may start the negotiations.

ГӮВ 

13. Negotiations ahead of the CouncilГўВҖВҷs first reading (Rule 73)
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ The SANT Committee has decided to enter into interinstitutional negotiations ahead of Council's first reading, pursuant to RuleГӮВ 73 of the Rules of Procedure.

The position adopted by Parliament at first reading, which constitutes the mandate for those negotiations, is available on the plenary webpage and its title will be published in the minutes of the sitting.

ГӮВ 

14. Delegated acts (Rule 114(6))
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ I was informed that no objections have been raised within the Conference of Committee Chairs to the recommendation by the AGRI Committee not to oppose a delegated act, pursuant to Rule 114(6) of our Rules. The recommendation is available on the plenary webpage.

If no objections are raised by a political group or Members reaching at least the low threshold within 24ГӮВ hours, the recommendation shall be deemed to have been approved.

ГӮВ 

15. Corrigenda (Rule 251)
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ The ECON Committee has transmitted a corrigendum to a text adopted by Parliament. Pursuant to Rule 251(1), this corrigendum will be deemed approved unless, no later than 24 hours after its announcement, a request is made by a political group or Members reaching at least the low threshold that it be put to the vote.

The corrigendum is available on the plenary webpage. Its title will be published in the minutes of this sitting.

ГӮВ 

16. Signature of acts adopted in accordance with the ordinary legislative procedure (Rule 81)
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ I would like to inform you that, since the adjournment of Parliament's session on 22ГӮВ May 2025, I have signed, together with the President of the Council, one act adopted under the ordinary legislative procedure, in accordance with Rule 81 of Parliament's Rules.

I would also like to inform you that tomorrow I shall sign, together with the President of the Council, five acts adopted under the ordinary legislative procedure.

The titles of the acts will be published in the minutes of this sitting.

ГўВҒВӮ

Now we move to the points of order. I have received 11, so we will go through them in the order that I received them.

As always, I ask you, please, dear colleagues, we know there's a little bit of flexibility on Mondays ГўВҖВ“ and it's also been a few weeks since we met in Strasbourg ГўВҖВ“ but it's becoming longer and longer. So, please, I ask you for responsibility.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ ГҺВ“ГҺВ№ГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВҪГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВңГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВ¬ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ (S&D). ГўВҖВ“ ГҺВҡГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВ ГҸВҒГҸВҢГҺВөГҺВҙГҸВҒГҺВө, ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҺВ»ГҺВҜГҺВіГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВІГҺВҙГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВөГҸВӮ, ГҺВјГҺВө ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢГҸВҶГҺВұГҸВғГҺВ· ГҺВұГҺВ№ГҺВіГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҚ ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВҝГҸВ…, ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВҷГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ¬ ГҺВңГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВ® ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВ‘ГҺВіГҺВҜГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВ‘ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВЈГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҺВ¬ ГўВҖВ”ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВұГҸВҒГҸВҮГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВҝ ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВҮГҸВҺГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВјГҺВөГҺВҪГҺВҝ ГҺВјГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ®ГҸВҒГҺВ№ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҸВҢГҸВғГҺВјГҺВҝГўВҖВ” ГҺВұГҸВҶГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВҒГҺВӯГҺВёГҺВ·ГҺВәГҺВө ГҺВ· ГҺВ№ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҺВәГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВғГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВҜГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВјГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҚ, ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВёГҸВҺГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВәГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВјГҺВөГҺВҪГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҺВіГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҺВҪ. ГҺВҲГҸВ„ГҸВғГҺВ№, ГҺВ· ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВңГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВҫГҺВұГҸВҒГҸВ„ГҺВ¬ГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВәГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ¬ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВ® ГҺВёГҺВӯГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВғГҺВ· ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВұГҺВ№ГҺВіГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҚ ГҺВәГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ, ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВҜГҺВҝ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВҖГҺВ»ГҺВӯГҺВҝГҺВҪ ГҺВҝ ГҺВ№ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҺВәГҸВ„ГҺВ®ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ. ГҺВҹГҺВ№ ГҺВјГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВұГҸВҮГҺВҝГҺВҜ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВҜ ГҸВҶГҺВ№ГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВҫГҺВөГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВјГҺВөГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВ№, ГҺВұГҸВҶГҺВҝГҸВҚ ГҸВғГҸВҮГҺВөГҺВҙГҸВҢГҺВҪ ГҸВҢГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВІГҸВҒГҺВҜГҸВғГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВөГҺВәГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВјГҺВө ГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВјГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВҪГҸВҢГҸВӮ ГҺВӯГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ. ГҺВ— ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢГҸВҶГҺВұГҸВғГҺВ· ГҺВұГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВ® ГҺВёГҺВӯГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҸВғГҺВө ГҺВәГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВҙГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВҝ ГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҺВІГҺВ№ГҸВүГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВјГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВұГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВҚ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВјГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҚ ГҺВјГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҚ, ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВӯГҸВҮГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВұ 15 ГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҺВҪГҸВүГҺВҪ.

ГҺВ©ГҸВӮ ГҸВғГҺВҝГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВұ, ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВёГҺВӯГҸВғГҺВұГҺВјГҺВө ГҺВұГҺВҜГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВұ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВ¶ГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВёГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВҹГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВӯГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВҡГҺВҝГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВІГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВ»ГҺВҜГҺВҝГҸВ…, ГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВ¬ ГҺВұГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҸВҢ ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҪ ГҺВ®ГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВҪ ГҺВҙГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВұГҸВ„ГҸВҢ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВұГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВ®ГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВөГҺВІГҺВҙГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВұ. ГҺВҳГҺВұ ГҺВөГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҺВјГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВјГҺВө, ГҸВҢГҺВјГҸВүГҸВӮ, ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВҹГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВӯГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВҷГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВ»ГҺВҜГҺВҝГҸВ…, ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВёГҸВҺГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВӯГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВөГҺВҫГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ¬ ГҸВғГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВұГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҢ ГҺВ¶ГҺВ®ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВұ, ГҺВ№ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВұГҺВҜГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВұ ГҺВјГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҸВҖГҺВ»ГҺВұГҺВҜГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВҝ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВјГҺВұГҺВәГҸВҒГҺВҝГҺВҝГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВІГҺВҝГҺВ®ГҺВёГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВ‘ГҺВҜГҺВіГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҸВ„ГҺВҝ.

ГўВҖВ“ ГҺВҡГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВ ГҸВҒГҸВҢГҺВөГҺВҙГҸВҒГҺВө, ГҺВұГҸВҚГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҝ ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВјГҸВҖГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҸВҺГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВөГҸВҖГҸВ„ГҺВ¬ ГҸВҮГҸВҒГҸВҢГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВјГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҺВҙГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВЈГҸВ…ГҺВјГҸВҶГҸВүГҺВҪГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҺВ ГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВғГҸВҖГҸВҺГҺВҪ, ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҺВӯГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВұГҸВҲГҺВұГҺВҪ ГҸВҮГҺВӯГҸВҒГҺВ№-ГҸВҮГҺВӯГҸВҒГҺВ№ ГҺВӨГҸВғГҺВҜГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВҡГҺВұГҺВјГҺВјГҺВӯГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВӮ. ГҺВ©ГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ®ГҸВҶГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВ· ГҺВңГҺВұГҺВәГҺВөГҺВҙГҸВҢГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВғГҺВұ, ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҪ ГҺВӯГҸВҮГҸВү ГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҺВјГҺВөГҺВіГҺВұГҺВ»ГҸВҚГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ· ГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВ® ГҺВұГҸВҖГўВҖВҷ ГҸВҢ,ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ ГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВіГҺВҪГҸВҺГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВ· ГҺВјГҺВұГҺВәГҺВөГҺВҙГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВіГҺВ»ГҸВҺГҸВғГҸВғГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВөГҺВёГҺВҪГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВЈГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВҚГҸВӮ ГўВҖВ”ГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВҝГҸВҚГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВҪ ГҺВ· ГҺВ’ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВ»ГҺВіГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҪ ГҺВҙГҺВӯГҸВҮГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВәГҺВө ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВӯ.

ГҺВ•ГҺВјГҺВөГҺВҜГҸВӮ, ГҺВөГҸВҖГҸВ„ГҺВ¬ ГҸВҮГҸВҒГҸВҢГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҸВҺГҸВҒГҺВұ, ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВөГҺВәГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ¬ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВұГҺВјГҺВұГҸВҒГҸВ„ГҸВҚГҸВҒГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВёГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВҮГҺВөГҺВҜГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВҝГҺВәГҺВ»ГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҺВЈГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВҜГҸВүГҺВҪ, ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВІГҺВ№ГҺВ¬ГҺВ¶ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВјГҸВҶГҸВүГҺВҪГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҸВғГҺВө ГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҺВёГҺВө ГҺВөГҸВҖГҺВҜГҸВҖГҺВөГҺВҙГҺВҝ ГўВҖВ”ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҢ, ГҺВұГҺВёГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҢ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҢ. ГҺВҹ ГҺВҡГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВ¬ГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВӮ ГҺВңГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҸВғГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ¬ГҺВәГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҸВҮГҺВө ГҺВҙГҺВөГҸВғГҺВјГҺВөГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВҙГҺВ·ГҺВјГҸВҢГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҸВүГҸВӮ, ГҺВұГҺВҪ ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВјГҸВҶГҸВүГҺВҪГҺВ·ГҺВёГҺВӯГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұ, ГҺВёГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№. ГҺВҲГҺВҫГҺВ№ ГҸВҮГҸВҒГҸВҢГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҸВҺГҸВҒГҺВұ, ГҺВҝГҸВҚГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҺВјГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВіГҺВіГҺВөГҺВ»ГҺВҜГҺВұ, ГҺВҝГҸВҚГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҺВјГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВ»ГҺВӯГҺВҫГҺВ·. ГҺВЈГҺВ№ГҸВүГҸВҖГҺВ® ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҸВҚГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҝ ГҺВ”ГҺВӯГҺВҪГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВұ. ГҺВҡГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВҝ ГҺВҶГҺВҙГҸВүГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВ“ГҺВөГҸВүГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВ·ГҸВӮ, ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҺВҙГҺВ®ГҺВ»ГҸВүГҺВҪГҺВө ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ№ ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҪ ГҺВёГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВӯГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВӯ ГӮВ«ГҺВ’ГҸВҢГҸВҒГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВңГҺВұГҺВәГҺВөГҺВҙГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВҜГҺВұГӮВ», ГҸВғГҺВ®ГҺВјГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВјГҸВҢГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВҪ ГҺВӯГҸВ„ГҸВғГҺВ№.

ГҺВ”ГҺВҜГҺВҪГҸВү ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҺВҪ ГҺВ»ГҸВҢГҺВіГҺВҝ ГҺВјГҺВҝГҸВ…, ГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВ№ГҸВҖГҸВҢГҺВҪ, ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ®ГҸВҶГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВңГҺВұГҺВәГҺВөГҺВҙГҸВҢГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВӮ, ГҸВҖГҸВүГҸВӮ ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВҪ ГҺВјГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВҙГҺВҝГҺВёГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВ· ГҺВҙГҸВҚГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВјГҺВ·, ГҺВёГҺВұ ГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВ·ГҺВёГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВұГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВ® ГҺВ· ГҺВөГҺВёГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ¬ ГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҸВүГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВјГҸВҶГҸВүГҺВҪГҺВҜГҺВұ. ГҺВ— ГҺВңГҺВұГҺВәГҺВөГҺВҙГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВјГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВөГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ®.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Sebastian Tynkkynen (ECR). ГўВҖВ“ Madam President, referring to Rule 10(3) of the Rules of Procedure, I would like to bring to your attention to the fact that equal treatment of Members was not upheld during the last plenary session concerning the IsraelГўВҖВ‘Gaza debate.

My ECR colleague Kristoffer StormГӮВ had a very small pin removed from his jacket ГўВҖВ“ a pin calling for the release of hostages kidnapped by Hamas who had been tortured and raped.

Meanwhile, when MEP Lynn Boylan from The Left Group approached the podium to deliver her speech wearing a Palestine lanyard, it was not removed. And this despite the fact that I had informed the President well in advance that the MEP in question would soon be speaking and was wearing that lanyard.

She was allowed to wear that political symbol throughout her entire speech and only after she had finished did the President simply remark that political symbols are not permitted while speaking.

How can it be that some MEPs are stripped of political expressions while others are not?

The plenary is the most sacred arena of democracy in the European Parliament. That is why I urge the President to ensure that Members are treated equally in the future and that such blatant double standards become a thing of the past.

18. Statement by the President - 40th anniversary of the Schengen area agreement
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ President. ГўВҖВ“ The next item is a statement and a group of speakers on the 40thГӮВ anniversary of the Schengen Agreement.

This past Saturday, 14ГӮВ June 2025, marked 40ГӮВ years since the signing of the agreement that established the Schengen area ГўВҖВ“ a defining achievement of European unity, of cooperation and freedom. What began in 1985 with just five countries has grown into the largest free travel area in the world, making life easier for over 400ГӮВ million people across the European Union, as well as in Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland.

This year, we warmly welcomed Bulgaria and Romania into our Schengen family, which is now made up of 29ГӮВ countries. It was a long-awaited step towards a more united, prosperous and secure Union. And work continues to extend those same benefits to all Member States.

Today, the Schengen area allows 3.5ГӮВ million people each day to cross internal borders freely ГўВҖВ“ to live, love, work and explore Europe without barriers. It boosts our economy by making trade between countries easier, cutting red tape for businesses and helping our single market work better.

Schengen, as I'm sure we'll hear throughout this debate, also makes us safer. It helps to keep us safe through closer cooperation between police, customs and border authorities to protect our borders and fight crime.

Around the world, the Schengen area is looked at with admiration, and it's really a clear and tangible example of what European cooperation can achieve.

But we should never take it for granted, because the preservation and the strengthening of Schengen takes constant commitment and effort from all of us. So this Parliament will keep working with Member States and the other EU institutions to modernise and to reinforce the Schengen area so that it stays fit for the future and true to its promise: that we always achieve more together than alone.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Tomas TobГғВ©, on behalf of the PPE Group. ГўВҖВ“ MadamГӮВ President, colleagues, the Schengen Area is one of the EU's greatest achievements. ГӮВ ГӮВ 

PRГғВүSIDENCE: YOUNOUS OMARJEE
Vice-PrГғВ©sident

ГӮВ 

19. State of play and follow-up two years after the PEGA recommendations and the illegal use of spyware (debate)
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Le PrГғВ©sident. ГўВҖВ“ Mes chers collГғВЁgues, l'ordre du jour appelle ГғВ  prГғВ©sent le dГғВ©bat sur les dГғВ©clarations du Conseil et de la Commission sur l'ГғВ©tat des lieux et les actions de suivi deux ans aprГғВЁs les recommandations de la commission d'enquГғВӘte PEGA et l'utilisation illГғВ©gale de logiciels espions [2025/2741(RSP)].

Je souhaite la bienvenue, au nom du Parlement, ГғВ  Monsieur le ministre des affaires europГғВ©ennes, au nom du Conseil, AdamГӮВ SzГ…ВӮapka, ГғВ  qui je donne la parole immГғВ©diatement.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Adam SzГ…ВӮapka, President of the European Council. ГўВҖВ“ Mr President, Madam Commissioner, honourable Members, let me start by thanking the Parliament for this debate.

The EU institutions and Member States have a joint responsibility to uphold the fundamental values on which the Union is based. It is clear that unjustified and disproportionate interference with individuals' fundamental rights are not acceptable. We need to ensure that any limitations of fundamental rights are applied under very strict conditions. Furthermore, democracy is based on the exercise of the right to freedom of opinion and expression, and the freedom of information. We must create an environment that protects journalists and media professionals in delivering on these rights.

The EU Media Freedom Act contributes to such an environment. The illegal use of spyware also highlights the importance of developing measures to protect our cybersecurity. The Cyber Resilience Act is an important step in this regard, but we also need preventive measures to ensure individual protection by raising awareness among individuals on the existing risks.

Enhancing democratic resilience has been one of the Polish presidency's priorities. The Council remains committed to tackling the current threats to our democratic institutions, as well as to strengthening the role of civil society in this process.ГӮВ This is an issue at the core of the recent presidential conclusions on strengthening EU democratic resilience. I am looking forward to the European Democracy Shield proposals to be put forward by the Commission later this year.

In conclusion, let me refer back to the joint responsibility which the EU institutions and Member States have on these issues. On the one hand, it is the responsibility of the Commission to oversee and assess the implementation of acceptable EU law. On the other, each Member State must also carry out investigations regarding possible illegal surveillance in accordance with Union and national law.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Henna Virkkunen, Executive Vice-President of the Commission. ГўВҖВ“ MrГӮВ President, honourable Members, thank you for putting this very crucial issue on the plenary agenda.

The Commission strongly condemns any illegal access to interpersonal communications and other data stored on user devices. Any illegal access to the data of our citizens, including journalists and political opponents, is unacceptable. It undermines our core European values, such as the fundamental rights to privacy and data protection.

The Commission has been looking at the illegal use of spyware from various angles of the EU law. It is important to address spyware in a holistic way because it poses challenges in many ways. First, in terms of rule of law and fundamental rights, but also data protection, media freedom, trade, cybersecurity, foreign interference and manipulation of information.

Some of these issues have already been addressed through legislation adopted by the Parliament and the Council. Others are addressed through nonГўВҖВ‘legislative tools. So what other existing measures do we have?

First, our data protection rules. They are very clear. They ensure that personal data is processed lawfully, fairly and in a transparent manner. They also limit personal data collection for specified, explicit and legitimate purposes.

Second, the European Media Freedom Act is another important part of our legal framework. It includes safeguards to protect journalists' sources and conventional communications against the illegal use of spyware. These rules on media freedom will enter into application this August.

They also include a general prohibition for intrusive surveillance software in devices used by media service providers, including journalists and related persons. We are currently working with Member States to ensure proper implementation of this and other provisions.

And third, in addition, we continue to report ГўВҖВ“ when appropriate ГўВҖВ“ on the issue of spyware, also in the annual Rule of Law report from the perspective of checks and balances and the protection of journalists.

In addition, the ePrivacy Directive prohibits the interception of communications as well as the access to and storage of information on user devices without their consent. Moreover, there is the Cyber Resilience Act, which sets cybersecurity requirements for hardware and software placed on the EU market. It introduces obligations for manufacturers, which will help to reduce system vulnerabilities often exploited by spyware.

It's also important to note that the investigations into the earliest misuse of spyware are a matter for national authorities, not for the Commission. And we expect, of course, national authorities to examine to the core any spyware allegations.

We have also been following with the European External Action Service the Pall Mall Process. This is an international initiative addressing various aspects related to the use of commercial cyber intrusion capabilities. We see this as a very important initiative, the first of its kind at international level and with a very broad scope. Many Member States have already committed to the Pall Mall Process. We are now carefully also exploring options for any further action to decide on the most appropriate way forward.

It's important to underline that we must, however, clearly separate the illegal use of spyware from the lawful access to data for law enforcement authorities. When law enforcement authorities use spyware for their purposes, the Law Enforcement Directive applies.

We must also acknowledge matters of national security, which are the responsibility of the Member States. However, in line with the case law of the Court of Justice, it is not possible for Member States to invoke national security in a general way. Member States must be able to demonstrate that national security would be compromised in the specific circumstances.

Furthermore, the legal use of spyware is only acceptable if it is non-discriminatory, justified by an overriding reason of public interest, proportionate and also in compliance with legal certainty and also our Charter of Fundamental Rights. And we expect, of course, national authorities to examine any allegations of illegal use of spyware as this is their responsibility.

So, honourable Members, the Commission and the co-legislators have in recent years addressed the multiple issues of spyware. This Parliament has played a key role in this process. The issue remains complex and further work is needed here, also in view of the changing security landscape and also the emergence of new technologies.ГӮВ The recommendations of the European Parliament's PEGA Committee have been very helpful to guide this work. I can assure you that the Commission is determined to protect the fundamental rights of our citizens to privacy, data protection and security.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Jeroen Lenaers, on behalf of the PPE Group. ГўВҖВ“ Mr President, Madam Executive Vice-President, imagine for a moment that someone is reading every message you've ever sent. Somebody is watching every video you've ever watched, listening into your private conversations with your children, your doctor, your partner. And this isn't fiction. It's happening also today. Also in Europe.

Spyware like Pegasus doesn't just intercept data, it invades our dignity. And yes, there can be, of course, exceptional circumstances where it can be used by authorities to fight terrorism, to fight serious organised crime. But what we've learned in this Parliament after speaking to over 200 people, numerous fact finding missions and several elaborate studies is that, also in the EU, it is abused by certain Member States to spy on opposition colleagues, to spy on journalists, and to spy on activists.

And it requires a strong response because this is not only about national security, it is also about protecting the rule of law and the EU and the European Commission. It has a role. It has competences when it comes to protecting the rule of law. Even better, we have a responsibility to do so.

And we also know what to do because our recommendations were very clear. Set up effective a democratic and judicial oversight mechanism, as well as provide citizens with access to legal remedies, regulate the trade in and the use of spyware based on the conditions that we have formulated together here, make sure that the invocation of national security is indeed always subject to independent review and oversight, and several more recommendations. They're all there.

What we need is action. And this is where I am a little bit disappointed in the European Commission. Two years ago, the Commission, in its response to our investigation, said that they were exploring the possibility of a non-legislative initiative. Now, this doesn't sound very ambitious in itself, but still you managed to overpromise and under deliver.

Sadly, I have to conclude that the previous Commission did not do its job in this regard. So I'm really counting on you also, Executive Vice-President Virkkunen, to make a difference here. ГҺВӨГҺВұ ГҺВ»ГҸВҢГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВҝГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВӯГҺВҫГҺВҝГҺВҙГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҸВҒГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВҪ ГҸВҖГҺВ»ГҺВӯГҺВҝГҺВҪ. ГҺВӨГҺВҝ ГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВіГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҢ Predator ГҺВөГҺВҫГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВёГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҸВҮГҸВҒГҺВ·ГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВјГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ№ГҺВөГҺВҜГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВөГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВ¬. ГҺВңГҺВ¬ГҺВёГҺВұГҺВјГҺВө ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ Graphite, ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВҜГҺВҝ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВөГҺВҫГҺВӯГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҺВҫГҺВ· ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… Pegasus ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВ„ГҸВҚГҸВҮГҺВёГҺВ·ГҺВәГҺВө ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВ·ГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҺВ® NSO. ГҺВ•ГҺВҙГҸВҺ, ГҺВҝ ГҺВҜГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВӮ ГҺВҝ ГҺВҷГҸВғГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВ·ГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҸВҢГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВӯГҸВғГҺВІГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВҷГҸВғГҸВҖГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВҝГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВҙГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВҜГҺВ·ГҸВғГҺВө ГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВғГҸВҢ ГҺВёГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҸВғГҺВҝГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҸВҮГҸВҺГҸВҒГҺВұ ГҺВјГҺВө ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ»ГҸВҚГҸВҲГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВёГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВӮ, ГҺВөГҸВҖГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВҙГҺВ® ГҺВ· ГҺВҷГҸВғГҸВҖГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВіГҺВҪГҸВҺГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВ ГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВ·. MoГ…Вјe na poczГ„В…tek mojemu rozentuzjazmowanemu przedmГғВіwcy z Polski mogГ„Вҷ odpowiedzieГ„ВҮ polskim przysГ…ВӮowiem: ГўВҖВһDiabeГ…ВӮ w ornat siГ„Вҷ ubraГ…ВӮ i ogonem na mszГ„Вҷ dzwoniГўВҖВқ. Zarzuty wobec Polski od poczГ„В…tku byГ…ВӮy politycznГ„В… kreacjГ„В…. DziaГ…ВӮania, ktГғВіre byГ…ВӮy podejmowane przez polskie sГ…ВӮuГ…Вјby, zawsze byГ…ВӮy podejmowane pod nadzorem sГ„В…dГғВіw i wymierzone byГ…ВӮy wobec osГғВіb, ktГғВіre realnie stanowiГ…ВӮy zagroГ…Вјenie dla bezpieczeГ…В„stwa paГ…В„stwa, albo wobec osГғВіb, ktГғВіre byГ…ВӮy podejrzane o dziaГ…ВӮania przestГ„Вҷpcze.

Najlepszym przykГ…ВӮadem jest tu osoba rosyjskiego szpiega GRU PawГ…ВӮa Rubcowa, ktГғВіry dziaГ…ВӮaГ…ВӮ pod przykryciem hiszpaГ…В„skiego dziennikarza, a jego zatrzymanie spowodowaГ…ВӮo wrГ„Вҷcz histeriГ„Вҷ, rГғВіwnieГ…Вј w tej Izbie, i przedstawiane byГ…ВӮo przez lewicowy establishment, jako przykГ…ВӮad represji rzГ„В…du PiS wobec dziennikarzy. Ten dziennikarz okazaГ…ВӮ siГ„Вҷ bardzo groГ…Вәnym szpiegiem, a ci, ktГғВіrzy brali go w obronГ„Вҷ, po raz kolejny okazali siГ„Вҷ poГ…Вјytecznymi idiotami Putina.

Ale, Szanowni PaГ…В„stwo, o hipokryzji i podwГғВіjnych standardach Г…Вӣwiadczy to, Г…Вјe instytucje Unii Europejskiej nie reagujГ„В… dzisiaj na Г…ВӮamanie praw podstawowych w Polsce przez obecny rzГ„В…d Tuska za naruszenie fundamentalnych elementГғВіw demokracji, chociaГ…Вјby za nielegalne zajГ„Вҷcie mediГғВіw publicznych i finansowanie kampanii wyborczej w Polsce przez oГ…Вӣrodki polityczne spoza Unii Europejskiej, przestГ„Вҷpcze wstrzymanie finansowania najwiГ„Вҷkszej partii opozycyjnej. JesteГ…Вӣcie hipokrytami.

ГӮВ ГӮВ Leoluca Orlando (Verts/ALE). ГўВҖВ“ Signor Presidente, onorevoli colleghi, signora Commissaria, grazie per aver ammesso che la Commissione nulla ha fatto dopo richieste e denunce sul caso Pegasus.

Grazie per aver ammesso che nulla inoltre risulta la Commissione ha fatto su ostacoli e condizionamenti da parte del governo italiano contro la libertГғВ  dei giornalisti, certificati al report Brunner 2024 sulГӮВ Rule of Law. Legga il report del 2024, signora Commissaria. Nulla la Commissione continua a fare sulle accertate responsabilitГғВ  del governo italiano che ha sostanzialmente autorizzato lo spionaggio da parte della societГғВ  israeliana Paragon di operatori sociali, responsabili soltanto di salvare vite umane nel Mediterraneo e avrebbe fatto avere le intercettazioni ai criminali libici finanziati dal governo italiano e guidati dal torturatore Almasri, esponendo quegli operatori sociali a rappresaglie di ogni genere.

Il governo italiano risulta ancora avere impedito alla societГғВ  Paragon, che ha denunciato ciГғВІ formalmente, di individuare gliГӮВ spyware mercenari che hanno spiato i giornalisti italiani. Nessuna contestazione, nessuna procedura di infrazione da parte della Commissione, pur dopo tante denunce e tante affermazioni. Signora Commissaria, la cosiddetta relazione Copasir, provi a leggerla e vedrГғВ , da questa relazione l'imbarazzante contraddizione di dover ammettere quello che ho appena finito di affermare.

ГӮВ ГӮВ Konstantinos Arvanitis (The Left). ГўВҖВ“ ГҺВҡГҸВҚГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВө ГҺВ ГҸВҒГҸВҢГҺВөГҺВҙГҸВҒГҺВө, ГҺВәГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҺВ•ГҸВҖГҺВҜГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВө, ГҺВјГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ№ ГҺВӯГҸВҮГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВјГҺВө ГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҸВҖГҺВ¬ГҸВҒГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҸВҚ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВ® ГҺВҙГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВ¬. ГҺВЈГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҸВ…ГҸВҮГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВҖГҺВ¬ГҸВҒГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҸВҚ. ГҺВҡГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҺВұГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВ® ГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҺВҙГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВ¬; ГҺВ‘ГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҸВҢ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВјГҺВөГҺВіГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВҝ ГҺВөГҸВҒГҸВҺГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВұ. ГҺВЈГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВұГҸВғГҺВјГҺВӯГҺВҪГҺВ· ГҺВёГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВұ ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВұГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВөГҺВҫГҺВөГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВөГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВ®, ГҺВІГҺВіГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВұГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВҜГҸВғГҺВјГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВұ, ГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ®ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҸВҚ, ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ 2025 ГҺВӯГҸВҮГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ Paragon ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВҷГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВҜГҺВұ.

ГҺВқГҺВұ ГҸВғГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВҪГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВөГҸВҒГҸВҺГҸВғГҸВү ГҸВҖГҸВүГҸВӮ ГҺВ· ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВӯГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВ•ГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВұ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҸВғГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВҙГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВҝ ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВёГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВөГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҺВјГҺВӯГҸВғГҸВү ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВіГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҚ Predator ГҺВөГҺВҫГҺВөГҺВ»ГҺВҜГҸВғГҸВғГҺВөГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВғГҺВө ГҺВёГҺВөГҸВғГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҸВүГҺВҙГҺВҜГҺВұ. ГҺВҹ ГҺВұГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВұГҺВіГҺВіГҺВөГҺВ»ГҺВӯГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВ‘ГҸВҒГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВ ГҺВ¬ГҺВіГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВӯГҺВәГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВө ГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҺВёГҺВө ГҺВөГҸВ…ГҺВёГҸВҚГҺВҪГҺВ· ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВ•ГҺВёГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВҘГҸВҖГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВғГҺВҜГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВ ГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҶГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҺВҪ, ГҺВ· ГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВҜГҺВұ ГўВҖВ”ГҺВ¬ГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВғГҺВҝГҺВҪ, ГҺВ¬ГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВғГҺВҝГҺВҪГўВҖВ” ГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҺВ¬ГҺВіГҺВөГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВұГҸВҶГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВҝ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҸВүГҺВёГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВҝГҸВҚ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВ•ГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВұГҸВӮ, ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВҮГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВәГҸВ„ГҺВ®ГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВө ГӮВ«ГҸВғГҸВҚГҺВјГҸВҖГҸВ„ГҸВүГҸВғГҺВ·ГӮВ» ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ№ 27 ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҸВҢГҸВғГҸВүГҸВҖГҺВұ, ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВ¬ГҺВјГҺВөГҸВғГҺВ¬ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВҝГҺВҜ, ГҺВөГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҸВүГҺВІГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВӯГҸВӮ, ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВҜ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВҙГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВҝГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҸВҶГҺВҝГҺВ№, ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВёГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҸВҢГҸВҮГҸВҒГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ Predator ГҺВјГҺВө ГҺВөГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВ® ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВ•ГҺВёГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВҘГҸВҖГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВғГҺВҜГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВ ГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҶГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҺВҪ.

ГҺВ ГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВ¬ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ№ ГҺВөГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҸВҢГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВ№ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВҜГҸВғГҸВү ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВіГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҢ, ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВҙГҺВҜГҸВүГҺВҫГҺВө ГҺВјГҸВҢГҺВҪГҺВҝ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВјГҺВӯГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВұ. ГҺВ“ГҺВ№ГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВҜ; ГҺВ•ГҸВҖГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВҙГҺВ® ГҺВ· ГҺВҙГҺВҜГҸВүГҺВҫГҺВ· ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҚГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВұ ГҺВёГҺВұ ГҺВҝГҺВҙГҺВ·ГҺВіГҺВҝГҸВҚГҸВғГҺВө ГҸВғГҺВө ГҺВӯГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҺВөГҸВҶГҺВӯГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВәГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВ®, ГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВ· ГҺВәГҸВ…ГҺВІГҺВӯГҸВҒГҺВҪГҺВ·ГҸВғГҺВ· ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҪ ГҺВ®ГҺВёГҺВөГҺВ»ГҺВө.

ГҺВҲГҸВ„ГҸВғГҺВ№, ГҺВӯГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҺВјГҺВөГҺВіГҺВұГҺВ»ГҸВҚГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ¬ ГҸВғГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВҙГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВұ ГҺВӯГҺВәГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВө ГҸВҮГҸВүГҸВҒГҺВҜГҸВӮ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВӯ ГҸВғГҺВө ГҸВҮГҺВӯГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВәГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВ®. ГҺВӨГҺВҝ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВіГҺВјГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВ ГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҸВүГҺВҪГҺВҜГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВёГҺВұ ГҺВјГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҚГҸВғГҺВө, ГҺВІГҺВөГҺВІГҺВұГҺВҜГҸВүГҸВӮ, ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВёГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВ· ГҺВ•ГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВұ. ГҺВқГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВҜГҺВ¶ГҸВү ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ№ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВјГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҺВјГҺВөГҸВ„ГҺВӯГҸВүГҸВҒГҺВҝГҺВ№, ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВіГҺВјГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ¬, ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВјГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВҮГҸВҚГҸВҒГҸВүГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҺВ№ ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВҢГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҪ ГҺВ»ГҺВұГҺВјГҺВІГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҺВёГҺВӯГҸВғГҺВ· ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҺВҙГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВ¬ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ.

ГӮВ ГӮВ Henna Virkkunen, Executive Vice-President of the Commission. ГўВҖВ“ Mr President, honourable Members, thank you very much for this very topical debate; it clearly shows the complex nature of the illegal use of spyware we are facing.

Let me state again that the Commission's view is very clear here: any attempt to illegally access data of citizens, including journalists and political opponents, is unacceptable. We are determined to protect the fundamental rights of our citizens to privacy, data protection and security.

We already have many rules in place: we have data protection rules, we have the ePrivacy directive and, just recently, we have adopted the Media Freedom Act, that comes into force in August, and also the Cyber Resilience Act. So we have already many, many rules in place. But I very much agree with you that when we look at the security environment where we are, the attacks against our democracies and also the very fast development of different technologies, I see that it is also important to see that further work in this field is needed. I am very grateful for the support from Parliament.

ГӮВ 

20. The human cost of RussiaГўВҖВҷs war against Ukraine and the urgent need to end Russian aggression: the situation of illegally detained civilians and prisoners of war, and the continued bombing of civilians (debate)
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Le PrГғВ©sident. ГўВҖВ“ L'ordre du jour appelle ГғВ  prГғВ©sent le dГғВ©bat sur les dГғВ©clarations du Conseil et de la Commission sur le coГғВ»t humain de la guerre menГғВ©e par la Russie contre l'Ukraine et la nГғВ©cessitГғВ© urgente de mettre fin ГғВ  l'agression russe: la situation des civils dГғВ©tenus illГғВ©galement et des prisonniers de guerre, et la poursuite des bombardements de civils [2025/2710(RSP)].

Je vous rappelle ГғВ  la tribune, Monsieur le MinistreГӮВ SzГ…ВӮapka.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Adam SzГ…ВӮapka, President-in-Office of the Council. ГўВҖВ“ Mr President, madam Commissioner, honourable Members, our last discussion on the Russian aggression against Ukraine took place only a month ago. The EU has firmly and repeatedly condemned the Russian aggression as a manifest violation of the EU Charter and international law. It is a global security and stability threat reaching well beyond Europe's borders.

I take this opportunity to express my respect for this House. The very first resolution adopting during this term, last July, was on the need of EU continued support for Ukraine. It represented a strong political message from Parliament.

This unjustified war is especially tragic for the Ukrainian population. Let me recall the devastating impact of this brutal aggression on Ukraine. So many civilians and soldiers killed, millions of Ukrainians displaced or having fled abroad. Millions of Ukrainians lack basic humanitarian aid, especially food, water, healthcare, illegally detained civilians and numerous prisoners of war.

The fate of Ukrainian children who are lawfully deported and transferred to Russia and Belarus is particularly close to our hearts. The Council clearly expressed that Russia and Belarus must immediately ensure their safe return to Ukraine.

Let me be clear on the main topic of today's debate. Russia commits war crimes and crimes against humanity by executing Ukrainian prisoners of war, and by subjecting Ukrainian prisoners and civilians to torture and other inhuman treatment. The Council has been very explicit on this matter. No crime can remain unpunished and international humanitarian law must be respected at all items.

Last week we saw Ukraine brought home the bodies of 1212 soldiers killed in the war of aggression by Russia. Last week too, Russia and Ukraine exchanged dozens of prisoners fathers exchange of prisoners expected to take place soon. Furthermore, thousands of Ukrainian civilians are detained in Russia whose families do not even know about their fate.

But let us face the reality. Russia does not want peace. On the contrary, Russia is escalating its war in Ukraine. Rather than focusing on the Istanbul peace talks, Moscow has increased its large-scale attack on civilians in Kyiv and other Ukrainian cities. The situation is only worsening. This is why we should continue to call for a comprehensive, just and lasting peace based on the UN Charter and international law.

A full and unconditional ceasefire is essential to stop human suffering. It is also a precondition for meaningful peace talks. Ukraine has accepted it and now it is for Russia to do the same.

We need to act now to further support Ukraine and further put pressure on Russia. Our position is clear and consistent. Ukraine needs to be in a position of strength to be able to negotiate a sustainable, comprehensive and just peace.

We are ready to support this effort with the tools that the EU has at its disposal. It is why we will treat the 18 packages of sanctions against Russia as a priority in the last weeks of our presidency in the Council.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Marta Kos, Member of the Commission. ГўВҖВ“ MrГӮВ President, dear honourable Members, dear Minister Adam SzГ…ВӮapka, Russia's war of aggression against Ukraine has had a devastating impact ГўВҖВ“ the killing and suffering of civilians whose cities are subjected to air raids targeting civilian infrastructure; the suffering of those illegally detained by Russia, of prisoners of war, subjected to torture and inhuman treatment and of forcibly transferred Ukrainian children to Russia; the suffering of those who struggle to earn their living among war-induced hardship.

The Commission stands firm in its condemnation of the numerous well-documented violations of international humanitarian law by Russia. This principled position translates into concrete action in support of the efforts of Ukraine and other members of the international community to ensure accountability.

First, supporting the International Criminal Court in its ongoing investigations against Russian perpetrators of war crimes and crimes against humanity ГўВҖВ“ this has been possible since 2014, with Ukraine's recognition of the court's jurisdiction under Article 12(3) of the Rome Statute. This has become even more straightforward, with Ukraine having completed the ratification of the Rome Statute and becoming a full-fledged state party of the ICC on 1ГӮВ January this year ГўВҖВ“ a long-standing point of EU-Ukraine political dialogue and a commitment under the Association Agreement with the EU.

Second, supporting Ukraine's own capacity to prosecute war crimes and crimes against humanity ГўВҖВ“ as part of its commitments stemming from the ratification of the Rome Statute, Ukraine has recently adopted relevant amendments to its Criminal Code and Criminal Procedure Code. The EU has actively participated in the international Atrocity Crimes Advisory Group, which supports the office of the Prosecutor-General of Ukraine in investigating and prosecuting international crimes committed during Russia's full-scale invasion. The Commission also supports numerous non-governmental initiatives in Ukraine, engaged in activities such as on-the-ground documentation of atrocities, collection of witness testimonies and support to civilians illegally detained by Russia.

Third, given the current gap in the ICC's jurisdiction over Russia's crime of aggression against Ukraine, the Commission and the VP/HR, Kaja Kallas, have been actively involved in work on the establishment of the Special Tribunal for the Crime of Aggression against Ukraine. Most recently, VP/HR Kallas and Commissioner McGrath joined representatives of an international coalition of states gathered in the core group at their high-level meeting in Lviv on 9ГӮВ May, endorsing texts agreed by legal experts which will lead to the establishment of this tribunal. This text will subsequently be transformed into legal acts of the Council of Europe.

Fourth, the Commission supports efforts to establish an international claims commission for Ukraine. On 4ГӮВ February this year, the Commission adopted a recommendation to the Council in this regard.

Finally, let me stress that the human cost of this war goes beyond the immediate suffering. The war has left Ukraine with a diminished workforce and a severely strained economy. This will profoundly affect the country's ability to rebuild. Reconstruction is not just a financial task, it is a human one, and the long-term social and economic consequences must be acknowledged alongside the legal and political efforts. The Commission remains committed to engage in reforms that will enable rebuild the economy and infrastructure in Ukraine once the war is over, keeping rule of law in its very centre.

Next month, I will be in the Ukraine Recovery Conference in Rome, where I will also be discussing the human aspects of Ukraine's reconstruction ГўВҖВ“ because behind every shattered school, every ruined hospital and every empty village is a life interrupted, and it is in our responsibility to help restore the future they were forced to put on hold.

ГӮВ ГӮВ Marie-Agnes Strack-Zimmermann (Renew). ГўВҖВ“ Frau PrГғВӨsidentin, Herr Minister, Frau Kommissarin! Kateryna Korovina ist eine 28-jГғВӨhrige Ukrainerin aus der Region Luhansk. Sie wurde im MГғВӨrz letzten Jahres auf dem Weg zur Apotheke vom russischen Inlandsgeheimdienst verschleppt und ist jetzt in einer Haftanstalt im russischen Rostow am Don. Zu zehn Jahren Haft ist sie verurteilt worden, weil sie angeblich kleine Spenden an die ukrainischen StreitkrГғВӨfte ГғВјberwiesen haben soll. Und wГғВӨhrend der VerhГғВ¶re wurde sie unter Druck gesetzt, ein GestГғВӨndnis zu unterschreiben, um fГғВјr ein erzwungenes Propagandavideo gefilmt zu werden, in dem sie einen vorgehaltenen Text ablas. Vor Gericht widerrief sie mutig ihre Aussagen und erklГғВӨrte, diese seien unter psychischem und physischem Druck gemacht worden. Sie bekannte sich als nicht schuldig und schloss ihre ErklГғВӨrung mit einem selbstgeschriebenen Gedicht mit dem Titel ГўВҖВһHorror in meinem ZuhauseГўВҖВң.

Es ist gut, dass wir heute darГғВјber sprechen, denn die Opfer haben einen Namen; sie sind nicht anonym. Und diese Menschen in den besetzten Gebieten haben unsere Aufmerksamkeit genauso verdient wie all die Opfer in der Ukraine. Und mir wird schlecht, wenn ich dann am rechten Rand jemanden hГғВ¶re, der sich Soziologe nennt, wie hier das mit FГғВјГғВҹen getreten wird. Putin ist der Verbrecher und kein anderer mehr.

ГӮВ ГӮВ Virginijus SinkeviГ„ВҚius (Verts/ALE). ГўВҖВ“ Madam President, dear colleagues, every day Russia's war against Ukraine brings new pain. Civilians are killed in their homes, children lose their parents. Russian bombs hit schools, hospitals and energy plants. Cities are left in darkness and people continue to live in fear.

And the suffering does not end at the frontline. Thousands of civilians and prisoners of war are held illegally by Russian forces. Many of them face torture, abuse, rape and even execution, including children. At least 75 of those cases are documented, and this is not a single event. This is a systemic terror against Ukrainian people. And these are not just numbers. These are lives. So every attack, every act of cruelty is a crime against humanity.

But words are not enough. We must act. We must deliver aid, secure the immediate release of all detainees, support Ukraine's defence and demand accountability. The Council must tighten sanctions and close every loophole that fuels Russia's war machine. The world cannot be silent. The human cost is too high. And it's time to bring justice to Ukraine.

ГӮВ ГӮВ Jonas SjГғВ¶stedt (The Left). ГўВҖВ“ Fru talman! Under de senaste veckorna har det gjorts fГғВ¶rsГғВ¶k att starta fredsfГғВ¶rhandlingar, men Ryssland vill inte ha fred. Ryssland svarar med brutala angrepp mot civila i Ukraina som aldrig tidigare. Ryssland avvisar Ukrainas erbjudande om vapenvila.

I stГғВӨllet har Ryssland nu, enligt president Zelenskyj, frГғВӨckheten att fГғВ¶reslГғВҘ att ryska krigsfГғВҘngar ska bytas mot kidnappade ukrainska barn. SГғВҘ argumenterar en imperialistisk regim som ГғВӨr moraliskt bankrutt.

StГғВӨllda infГғВ¶r de hГғВӨr provokationerna och stГғВӨllda infГғВ¶r USA:s vГғВӨgran att stГғВ¶dja Ukraina, ГғВӨr det vГғВҘr uppgift att ГғВ¶ka stГғВ¶det ГўВҖВ“ ГғВ¶ka det ekonomiska stГғВ¶det, ГғВ¶ka det politiska stГғВ¶det och ГғВ¶ka det militГғВӨra stГғВ¶det som gГғВ¶r att Ukraina kan befria sina ockuperade omrГғВҘden och fortleva som en demokratisk, oberoende nation.

ГӮВ ГӮВ Petar Volgin (ESN). ГўВҖВ“ ГҗВ“-ГҗВ¶ГҗВҫ ГҗВҹГ‘ВҖГҗВөГҗВҙГ‘ВҒГҗВөГҗВҙГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВөГҗВ», ГҗВіГҗВ»ГҗВ°ГҗВІГҗВҪГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө ГҗВІГҗВёГҗВҪГҗВҫГҗВІГҗВҪГҗВёГ‘ВҶГҗВё ГҗВ·ГҗВ° ГҗВҝГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВҙГ‘ВҠГҗВ»ГҗВ¶ГҗВ°ГҗВІГҗВ°ГҗВҪГҗВөГ‘ВӮГҗВҫ ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВІГҗВҫГҗВ№ГҗВҪГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВ° ГҗВІ ГҗВЈГҗВәГ‘ВҖГҗВ°ГҗВ№ГҗВҪГҗВ° Г‘ВҒГҗВө ГҗВҪГҗВ°ГҗВјГҗВёГ‘ВҖГҗВ°Г‘ВӮ ГҗВІ ГҗВ‘Г‘ВҖГ‘ВҺГҗВәГ‘ВҒГҗВөГҗВ». ГҗВ Г‘ВҠГҗВәГҗВҫГҗВІГҗВҫГҗВҙГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВөГҗВ»ГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВ•ГҗВІГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВҝГҗВөГҗВ№Г‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВёГ‘ВҸ Г‘ВҒГ‘ВҠГ‘ВҺГҗВ· ГҗВҝГҗВҫГ‘ВҒГ‘ВӮГҗВҫГ‘ВҸГҗВҪГҗВҪГҗВҫ ГҗВ·ГҗВ°ГҗВұГҗВ»Г‘ВғГҗВ¶ГҗВҙГҗВ°ГҗВІГҗВ°Г‘ВӮ Г‘ВғГҗВәГ‘ВҖГҗВ°ГҗВёГҗВҪГ‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВёГ‘ВҸ ГҗВҪГҗВ°Г‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВҙ, Г‘ВҮГҗВө ГҗВө ГҗВІГ‘ВҠГҗВ·ГҗВјГҗВҫГҗВ¶ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВҝГҗВҫГҗВұГҗВөГҗВҙГҗВ° Г‘ВҒГ‘ВҖГҗВөГ‘ВүГ‘Вғ ГҗВ Г‘ВғГ‘ВҒГҗВёГ‘ВҸ, Г‘ВҮГҗВө ГҗВҙГҗВҫГ‘ВҖГҗВё ГҗВё ГҗВЎГ‘ВҠГҗВөГҗВҙГҗВёГҗВҪГҗВөГҗВҪГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө Г‘ВүГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВё ГҗВҙГҗВ° ГҗВҫГ‘ВӮГ‘ВӮГҗВөГҗВіГҗВ»Г‘ВҸГ‘ВӮ ГҗВҝГҗВҫГҗВҙГҗВәГ‘ВҖГҗВөГҗВҝГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВ° Г‘ВҒГҗВё ГҗВ·ГҗВ° ГҗВҡГҗВёГҗВөГҗВІ, ГҗВ•ГҗВІГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВҝГҗВөГҗВ№Г‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВёГ‘ВҸГ‘ВӮ Г‘ВҒГ‘ВҠГ‘ВҺГҗВ· Г‘ВүГҗВө ГҗВҝГ‘ВҖГҗВөГҗВҙГҗВҫГ‘ВҒГ‘ВӮГҗВ°ГҗВІГҗВё Г‘ВҒГ‘ВҠГ‘ВүГҗВҫ Г‘ВӮГҗВҫГҗВ»ГҗВәГҗВҫГҗВІГҗВ°, ГҗВ°ГҗВәГҗВҫ ГҗВҪГҗВө ГҗВё ГҗВҝГҗВҫГҗВІГҗВөГ‘ВҮГҗВө ГҗВҝГҗВ°Г‘ВҖГҗВё ГҗВё ГҗВҫГ‘ВҖГ‘ВҠГҗВ¶ГҗВёГ‘ВҸ ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВ—ГҗВөГҗВ»ГҗВөГҗВҪГ‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВё.

ГҗВ”Г‘ВҖГ‘ВғГҗВіГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВ° ГҗВіГҗВҫГҗВ»Г‘ВҸГҗВјГҗВ° ГҗВ»Г‘ВҠГҗВ¶ГҗВ°, ГҗВәГҗВҫГ‘ВҸГ‘ВӮГҗВҫ ГҗВ»ГҗВёГҗВҙГҗВөГ‘ВҖГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВ•ГҗВЎ ГҗВҪГҗВө Г‘ВҒГҗВҝГҗВёГ‘ВҖГҗВ°Г‘ВӮ ГҗВҙГҗВ° ГҗВҝГҗВҫГҗВІГ‘ВӮГҗВ°Г‘ВҖГ‘ВҸГ‘ВӮ, ГҗВө, Г‘ВҮГҗВө ГҗВёГҗВјГҗВ° ГҗВҪГ‘ВҸГҗВәГҗВ°ГҗВәГҗВІГҗВ° Г‘ВғГҗВ¶ГҗВ°Г‘ВҒГҗВҪГҗВ° Г‘ВҖГ‘ВғГ‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВ° ГҗВ·ГҗВ°ГҗВҝГҗВ»ГҗВ°Г‘В…ГҗВ° ГҗВё Г‘ВҮГҗВө ГҗВ°ГҗВәГҗВҫ ГҗВ Г‘ВғГ‘ВҒГҗВёГ‘ВҸ ГҗВҪГҗВө ГҗВұГ‘ВҠГҗВҙГҗВө Г‘ВҒГҗВҝГ‘ВҖГ‘ВҸГҗВҪГҗВ° Г‘ВҒГҗВөГҗВіГҗВ°, ГҗВІ Г‘ВҒГҗВ»ГҗВөГҗВҙГҗВІГҗВ°Г‘ВүГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө ГҗВіГҗВҫГҗВҙГҗВёГҗВҪГҗВё Г‘ВӮГ‘ВҸ Г‘ВүГҗВө ГҗВ·ГҗВ°ГҗВІГҗВ»ГҗВ°ГҗВҙГҗВөГҗВө Г‘ВҶГ‘ВҸГҗВ»ГҗВ° ГҗВ•ГҗВІГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВҝГҗВ°.

ГҗВ—ГҗВ°Г‘ВүГҗВҫ ГҗВөГҗВІГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВҪГҗВ°Г‘ВҮГҗВ°ГҗВ»ГҗВҪГҗВёГ‘ВҶГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө ГҗВіГҗВҫГҗВІГҗВҫГ‘ВҖГ‘ВҸГ‘ВӮ ГҗВҝГҗВҫГҗВҙГҗВҫГҗВұГҗВҪГҗВё ГҗВҫГҗВұГҗВёГҗВҙГҗВҪГҗВё ГҗВ·ГҗВ° ГҗВ·ГҗВҙГ‘ВҖГҗВ°ГҗВІГҗВёГ‘ВҸ Г‘ВҖГҗВ°ГҗВ·Г‘ВғГҗВј ГҗВіГҗВ»Г‘ВғГҗВҝГҗВҫГ‘ВҒГ‘ВӮГҗВё? ГҗВ—ГҗВ°Г‘ВүГҗВҫГ‘ВӮГҗВҫ Г‘ВҒГҗВ° Г‘ВғГҗВұГҗВөГҗВҙГҗВөГҗВҪГҗВё, Г‘ВҮГҗВө ГҗВ°ГҗВәГҗВҫ Г‘ВғГҗВҝГҗВ»ГҗВ°Г‘ВҲГҗВ°Г‘ВӮ ГҗВҙГҗВҫГ‘ВҒГ‘ВӮГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГ‘ВҠГ‘ВҮГҗВҪГҗВҫ Г‘ВҒГҗВёГҗВ»ГҗВҪГҗВҫ ГҗВөГҗВІГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВҝГҗВөГҗВ№Г‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө ГҗВҙГ‘ВҠГ‘ВҖГҗВ¶ГҗВ°ГҗВІГҗВё, Г‘ВӮГҗВөГҗВ·ГҗВё ГҗВҙГ‘ВҠГ‘ВҖГҗВ¶ГҗВ°ГҗВІГҗВё Г‘ВүГҗВө Г‘ВҒГҗВө Г‘ВҒГҗВІГҗВёГ‘ВҸГ‘ВӮ Г‘ВҒГ‘ВӮГ‘ВҖГҗВ°Г‘В…ГҗВ»ГҗВёГҗВІГҗВҫ ГҗВё ГҗВҝГҗВҫГҗВәГҗВҫГ‘ВҖГҗВҪГҗВҫ Г‘ВүГҗВө ГҗВёГҗВ·ГҗВҝГ‘ВҠГҗВ»ГҗВҪГ‘ВҸГҗВІГҗВ°Г‘ВӮ ГҗВ·ГҗВ°ГҗВҝГҗВҫГҗВІГҗВөГҗВҙГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВ‘Г‘ВҖГ‘ВҺГҗВәГ‘ВҒГҗВөГҗВ».

ГҗВ•ГҗВІГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВ»ГҗВёГҗВҙГҗВөГ‘ВҖГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө Г‘ВҒГҗВјГ‘ВҸГ‘ВӮГҗВ°Г‘ВӮ, Г‘ВҮГҗВө ГҗВҫГ‘ВӮГ‘ВӮГ‘ВғГҗВә-ГҗВҪГҗВ°Г‘ВҒГҗВөГ‘ВӮГҗВҪГҗВө Г‘ВүГҗВө ГҗВјГҗВҫГҗВіГҗВ°Г‘ВӮ ГҗВҙГҗВ° ГҗВҝГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВәГҗВ°Г‘ВҖГҗВ°Г‘ВӮ ГҗВІГ‘ВҒГ‘ВҸГҗВәГҗВ° ГҗВёГҗВҙГҗВёГҗВҫГ‘ВӮГ‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВ° ГҗВҝГҗВҫГҗВ»ГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВёГҗВәГҗВ° Г‘ВҒ ГҗВҫГҗВҝГ‘ВҖГҗВ°ГҗВІГҗВҙГҗВ°ГҗВҪГҗВёГҗВөГ‘ВӮГҗВҫ, Г‘ВҮГҗВө Г‘ВӮГ‘ВҸ ГўВҖВһГ‘ВҒГҗВҝГҗВ°Г‘ВҒГ‘ВҸГҗВІГҗВ° ГҗВ•ГҗВІГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВҝГҗВ° ГҗВҫГ‘ВӮ Г‘ВҖГ‘ВғГ‘ВҒГҗВҪГҗВ°Г‘ВҶГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВөГўВҖВң. ГҗВ•Г‘ВӮГҗВҫ ГҗВ·ГҗВ°Г‘ВүГҗВҫ ГҗВІГҗВёГ‘ВҒГ‘ВҲГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө ГҗВұГ‘ВҖГ‘ВҺГҗВәГ‘ВҒГҗВөГҗВ»Г‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВё ГҗВұГ‘ВҺГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВәГ‘ВҖГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВё, ГҗВ° ГҗВҪГҗВө ГҗВҫГҗВұГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВөГҗВ»ГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВө ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВҡГ‘ВҖГҗВөГҗВјГ‘ВҠГҗВ» Г‘ВҒГҗВ° ГҗВҫГ‘ВҒГҗВҪГҗВҫГҗВІГҗВҪГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВ° ГҗВҝГ‘ВҖГҗВөГ‘ВҮГҗВәГҗВ° ГҗВҝГ‘ВҖГҗВөГҗВҙ ГҗВҝГҗВҫГ‘ВҒГ‘ВӮГҗВёГҗВіГҗВ°ГҗВҪГҗВөГ‘ВӮГҗВҫ ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВјГҗВёГ‘ВҖ ГҗВІ ГҗВЈГҗВәГ‘ВҖГҗВ°ГҗВ№ГҗВҪГҗВ°.

ГҗВҗГҗВәГҗВҫ ГҗВ•ГҗВІГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВҝГҗВөГҗВ№Г‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВёГ‘ВҸГ‘ВӮ Г‘ВҒГ‘ВҠГ‘ВҺГҗВ· Г‘ВҒГҗВө Г‘ВҒГҗВіГ‘ВҖГҗВҫГҗВјГҗВҫГҗВ»Г‘ВҸГ‘ВҒГҗВ°, Г‘ВӮГҗВҫГҗВІГҗВ° Г‘ВүГҗВө ГҗВұГ‘ВҠГҗВҙГҗВө ГҗВҪГҗВө ГҗВ·ГҗВ°Г‘ВҖГҗВ°ГҗВҙГҗВё ГҗВҙГҗВөГҗВ№Г‘ВҒГ‘ВӮГҗВІГҗВёГ‘ВҸГ‘ВӮГҗВ° ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВңГҗВҫГ‘ВҒГҗВәГҗВІГҗВ°, ГҗВ° ГҗВ·ГҗВ°Г‘ВҖГҗВ°ГҗВҙГҗВё ГҗВҪГҗВөГҗВ°ГҗВҙГҗВөГҗВәГҗВІГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВҪГҗВ°Г‘ВӮГҗВ° ГҗВҝГҗВҫГҗВ»ГҗВёГ‘ВӮГҗВёГҗВәГҗВ° ГҗВҪГҗВ° ГҗВ‘Г‘ВҖГ‘ВҺГҗВәГ‘ВҒГҗВөГҗВ».

ГӮВ ГӮВ Г„ВҪuboГ…ВЎ Blaha (NI). ГўВҖВ“ VГғВЎГ…ВҫenГғВЎ pani predsedajГғВәca, vГғВЎГ…ВҫenГғВӯ kolegovia, to vГғВЎm naozaj neprГғВӯde trГғВЎpne, Г…Вҫe tu tГғВЎrate o sankciГғВЎch proti Rusku, ale nedokГғВЎГ…Вҫete ani len odsГғВәdiГ…ВҘ Izrael za to, Г…Вҫe napadol suverГғВ©nny IrГғВЎn a eГ…ВЎte aj pГғВЎcha genocГғВӯdu na palestГғВӯnskom nГғВЎrode? Kde sГғВә sankcie proti Izraelu, pani CallasovГғВЎ? Kde sГғВә dodГғВЎvky zbranГғВӯ pre IrГғВЎn? VojenskГғВЎ agresia odrazu nevadГғВӯ? 21. Strengthening rural areas in the EU through cohesion policy (debate)
Video of the speeches
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ PrzewodniczГ„В…ca. ГўВҖВ“ Kolejnym punktem porzГ„В…dku dziennego jest sprawozdanie sporzГ„В…dzone przez Denisa Nesciego w imieniu Komisji Rozwoju Regionalnego w sprawie wzmocnienia obszarГғВіw wiejskich UE dziГ„Вҷki polityce spГғВіjnoГ…Вӣci (2024/2105(INI)) (A10-0092/2025).

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Denis Nesci, relatore. ГўВҖВ“ Signora Presidente, onorevoli colleghi, signor Vicepresidente esecutivo Fitto, oggi ГғВЁ con profondo senso di responsabilitГғВ  e sincera emozione che mi rivolgo a voi per presentare la relazione sul rafforzamento delle zone rurali nell'Unione europea attraverso la politica di coesione.

Sono figlio di una terra che conosce bene le potenzialitГғВ  ma anche le difficoltГғВ  del mondo rurale. ГғВҲ proprio da questa consapevolezza che nasce il lavoro che oggi vi presento. La relazione vuole essere un punto di partenza per un'azione concreta verso ciГғВІ che dovrebbe essere un obiettivo condiviso da tutti noi: portare le zone rurali a essere non piГғВ№ marginali, ma finalmente protagoniste di una strategia di sviluppo mirata.

Le zone rurali coprono l'80 % del territorio europeo e ospitano quasi un quarto della popolazione. Eppure, sembra che non si sia mai pensato di svilupparle in modo parallelo alle zone urbane. Da troppo tempo queste aree soffrono di isolamento, spopolamento, scarsa connettivitГғВ , accesso limitato ai servizi essenziali, invecchiamento demografico e difficoltГғВ  occupazionali. Ma non sono terre perse, sono risorse preziose, scrigni di cultura, biodiversitГғВ , identitГғВ  e, oggi piГғВ№ che mai, leve strategiche per nuovi modi di produrre energia e per la sicurezza alimentare.

Il file nasce da questa convinzione: rilanciare le zone rurali non ГғВЁ solo un atto di giustizia territoriale, ГғВЁ una scelta strategica per l'intera Unione. ГғВҲ strategico, infatti, voler fornire alle aree rurali strumenti propri sia in termini finanziari che amministrativi. A questo proposito, la creazione di infopoint dedicati al supporto delle PMI e dei comuni risulta oggi imprescindibile per ottimizzare l'utilizzo delle risorse disponibili e garantire un sostegno concreto alle regioni.

Abbiamo lavorato con l'obiettivo di dare una cornice chiara e strumenti efficaci per valorizzare le aree rurali come motori di sviluppo. Il testo propone una strategia integrata che unisca politiche agricole, coesione territoriale, innovazione digitale, accesso ai trasporti, formazione, servizi idrici efficienti e sanitГғВ . In particolare sulla sanitГғВ  invitiamo la Commissione a integrare la sua strategia per la sanitГғВ  digitale, misure specifiche per le zone identificate come rurali nell'ottica di fornire ai presidi sanitari del territorio un supporto concreto per l'aggiornamento delle tecnologie, e chiediamo di potenziare i servizi offerti da tali presidi.

Sottolineiamo inoltre il ruolo centrale dello sviluppo infrastrutturale per la crescita economica e sociale delle zone rurali, vista la necessitГғВ  di sistemi di trasporto, in particolare quelli pubblici, che consentano collegamenti migliori e un migliore accesso ai servizi essenziali, ma anche la necessitГғВ  di reti energetiche piГғВ№ efficienti e resilienti.

Vogliamo che vivere in una zona definita "rurale" non significhi avere meno opportunitГғВ . Questo significa investire in infrastrutture, sostenere le imprese rurali, promuovere il turismo sostenibile, rafforzare la resilienza dei territori, incentivare il ruolo delle donne e il ritorno dei giovani alla loro terra. Il cuore pulsante della proposta ГғВЁ uno: la dignitГғВ  delle persone. Non possiamo accettare che vivere in un borgo o in una valle significhi essere cittadini di serie B. Ogni comunitГғВ  rurale ha diritto a servizi, connettivitГғВ , formazione e prospettive.

Il lavoro ГғВЁ frutto di un ascolto attento sui territori, attraverso gli incontri con gli agricoltori, gli amministratori locali, le associazioni, i giovani. Questo perchГғВ© le politiche rurali devono partire dal basso, rispettare il principio di sussidiarietГғВ , rafforzare l'identitГғВ  e la responsabilitГғВ  locale.

Sostenere le zone rurali non significa solo interpretare e ampliare il principio della politica di coesione, ma rappresenta un investimento concreto per il futuro dell'Europa. E poi ГғВЁ un segnale chiaro che rivolgiamo ai nostri cittadini: non vi abbiamo dimenticati. ГҗВҖ soprattutto un messaggio di speranza per chi vuole restare e ancor di piГғВ№ un riconoscimento del diritto dei nostri giovani di restare nella loro terra e costruire lГғВ¬ il proprio futuro.

Ringrazio tutti coloro che hanno contribuito, in particolare i relatori ombra, gli advisor, i tecnici, per l'efficace collaborazione e invito quest'Aula a far propria questa visione perchГғВ© centinaia di migliaia di comunitГғВ  rurali che aspettano da tempo un segnale chiaro dall'Europa non hanno piГғВ№ il tempo di aspettare.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Raffaele Fitto, Executive Vice-President of the Commission. ГўВҖВ“ MadamГӮВ President, honourable Members, first, I would like to thank rapporteur Nesci and all the shadow rapporteurs for this important and timely report.

I fully agree with your analysis. Rural areas are central to our European way of life, and they are essential for Europe's competitiveness and resilience. I welcome the report's recognition that cohesion policy plays a crucial role in strengthening rural areas.

Supporting rural areas is a high priority for the Commission. As rightly emphasised in the report, cohesion policy already delivers significant support in rural areas. This complements the rural development interventions provided by the common agricultural policy. Investment in broadband, transport, clean energy, small and medium enterprises and innovation, and in health, education and local infrastructure, enhances economic and social cohesion.

However, challenges like skills shortages, the digital divide, demographic decline and the limited access to essential services persist. As correctly underlined in the report, we need further efforts to provide our rural areas with adequate tools to overcome the considerable challenges they face, which have an increasing impact on regional competitiveness and social cohesion.

A particular priority for me is the right to stay ГўВҖВ“ the right of every European to remain in the place they call home. This is also fundamental for young generations of farmers, which is one of the key challenges in our farming sector. The Commission committed to further promote generational renewal in the agricultural sector through a dedicated strategy later this year.

Several regions in the EU are facing the problem of depopulation. This has led to a sharp decline for their working-age population. Apart from the tools under cohesion policy and the common agricultural policy, social policies and social innovation can help address this. Through the Harnessing Talent Platform, we are also actively working with 82ГӮВ regions, including 27ГӮВ mainly rural regions, to develop local strategies that retain talent and allow for smart adjustments to demographic challenges.

In addition, the mid-term review of cohesion policy programmes puts the focus on several areas of key concern for rural areas, providing incentives and flexibilities for goals such as water resilience, housing, energy transition and greater competitiveness innovation.

For example, water resilience ГўВҖВ“ we have seen regions facing water scarcity while others are affected by floods. Through the mid-term review, we propose changes to encourage investment in water resilience, including digitalisation of water infrastructure, and mitigation of drought and desertification impacts.

The mid-term review proposal will deliver a more responsive cohesion policy, aligned with today's realities, and better addressing current and future challenges.

Earlier this year, Commissioner Hansen and I presented the new Vision for Agriculture and Food, strengthening the synergies between policies to help rural areas, updating our rural action plan and further developing rural proofing, as well as the Rural Pact.

With this in mind, the Commission collaborates with the agrifood sector, ensuring that the sector remains competitive, resilient, attractive for future generations, and profitable.

Finally, you highlighted in your report the need to simplify administrative procedures by reducing red tape for farmers and small rural businesses. Here, I am happy to point out that in May, the European Commission adopted the omnibus proposal on agriculture, responding to the need to simplify the policy.

To conclude, this report makes a valuable contribution to the future of rural areas. Collaboration is key. We need to work together. This requires action and partnership across all levels of governance to modernise, simplify and reinforce the cohesion policy, providing tailored solutions to the unique situation of every territory in Europe, with the rural regions at the heart of our efforts.

I now look forward to the debate and to hearing your views.

ГӮВ ГӮВ

ГӮВ ГӮВ Cristina Guarda, relatrice per parere della commissione AGRI. ГўВҖВ“ Signora Presidente, onorevoli colleghi, innanzitutto vorrei ringraziare i colleghi con cui ho affrontato questo percorso sia nella commissione per l'agricoltura che nella commissione per lo sviluppo regionale, perchГғВ© finalmente si parla di utilizzare la politica di coesione per sostenere davvero le aree rurali, non soltanto in agricoltura, ma anche per garantire servizi essenziali, opportunitГғВ  per giovani, donne, genitori, o per investire nella transizione ecologica per difendere le piccole imprese dalla crisi climatica o progetti come le comunitГғВ  energetiche, che restituiscono potere ai cittadini.

De aceea spun cГ„Вғ trebuie sГ„Вғ gГғВўndim proiectele consolidat: infrastructurГ„Вғ, sГ„Вғ aibГ„Вғ medic, sГ„Вғ existe ГҲВҷcoalГ„Вғ, sГ„Вғ poatГ„Вғ sГ„Вғ aibГ„Вғ conexiune la internet. Sunt zone ГғВ®ntregi rurale ГғВ®n care nu existГ„Вғ posibilitatea de conectivitate.

Sper, domnule comisar, cГ„Вғ veГҲВӣi susГҲВӣine ca aceste zone rurale sГ„Вғ aibГ„Вғ bugete ГҲВӣintite, pentru cГ„Вғ dacГ„Вғ dГ„Вғm buget la grГ„ВғmadГ„Вғ ГҲВҷi mai este o problemГ„Вғ, s-a discutat aici, trebuie sГ„Вғ simplificГ„Вғm procedura de accesare a fondurilor de cГ„Вғtre administraГҲВӣiile din comunitГ„ВғГҲВӣile mici sau de cГ„Вғtre micii ГғВ®ntreprinzГ„Вғtori.

ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Sebastian Tynkkynen (ECR). ГўВҖВ“ Arvoisa puhemies, jokaista maksettua euroa kohti Suomi saa vain noin 20 senttiГғВӨ EU:lta takaisin. TГғВӨtГғВӨ tarkoittaa EU:n koheesiopolitiikka Suomelle. Onko tГғВӨssГғВӨ mitГғВӨГғВӨn jГғВӨrkeГғВӨ?

Suomella on piikki auki, oli sitten kyse jГғВӨttimГғВӨisestГғВӨ elpymispaketista tai joka vuosi jaettavista koheesiorahoista. Ja muut maat nauravat matkalla pankkiin. On aika alkaa vaatia.

Olen tyytyvГғВӨinen, ettГғВӨ komissio vihdoin ja viimein huomioi myГғВ¶s itГғВӨisen Suomen tulevassa koheesiopolitiikassaan. TГғВӨmГғВӨ ei kuitenkaan vielГғВӨ riitГғВӨ. EU:n itГғВӨisille alueille tarvitaan kokonaan oma rahoitusratkaisunsa ГўВҖВ“ ratkaisu, jossa rahat eivГғВӨt jГғВӨГғВӨ muiden kupattavaksi.

Suomi seisoo yli tuhannen kolmensadan kilometrin mittaisessa eturintamassa Euroopassa hyГғВ¶kkГғВӨГғВӨvГғВӨГғВӨ maata vastaan. Nyt ei ole meidГғВӨn aikamme maksaa muiden viuluja. Nyt on meidГғВӨn aikamme saada.

ГӮВ ГӮВ Oihane Agirregoitia MartГғВӯnez (Renew). ГўВҖВ“ SeГғВұor presidente, seГғВұor comisario, la extrema derecha crece en toda Europa y lo hace especialmente en las zonas rurales. Si queremos realmente actuar contra la extrema derecha y contra populismos, debemos actuar, y los fondos de cohesiГғВіn son clave para reducir desigualdades y para lanzar un mensaje claro a todas aquellas personas que quieren hacer su vida en entornos mГғВЎs allГғВЎ de los grandes nГғВәcleos urbanos.

Queremos y necesitamos una polГғВӯtica de cohesiГғВіn que sea moderna y que estГғВ© claramente orientada y unos fondos de cohesiГғВіn que estГғВ©n regionalizados y que nos permitan garantizar la cohesiГғВіn territorial y atacar las desigualdades. Esos son los dos condicionantes que vamos a vigilar para el nuevo diseГғВұo del marco financiero plurianual: regionalizaciГғВіn de la polГғВӯtica de cohesiГғВіn y autonomГғВӯa en la gestiГғВіn de los fondos para atacar el crecimiento de la extrema derecha.

ГӮВ ГӮВ Ana Miranda Paz (Verts/ALE). ГўВҖВ“ Senhor Presidente, Senhor ComissГғВЎrio, a polГғВӯtica de coesГғВЈo ГғВ© fundamental para garantirmos zonas rurais vivas e com serviГғВ§os bГғВЎsicos. Por isso, nГғВЈo concordamos que o governo europeu reoriente incorretamente os fundos para fins militares.

Na Galiza, o meu paГғВӯs, ainda se aguarda uma decisГғВЈo sobre o que financiar com 60 % dos fundos. 62 % dos municГғВӯpios galegos estГғВЈo designados como zonas desfavorecidas. O ГғВӘxodo rural avanГғВ§a de forma imparГғВЎvel na Galiza. Em apenas um ano, 32 aldeias ficaram desertas.

Temos escassez de serviГғВ§os bГғВЎsicos nas zonas rurais e muita emigraГғВ§ГғВЈo. As pessoas ficam se houver trabalho e serviГғВ§os.

Senhor ComissГғВЎrio, precisamos de um apoio especГғВӯfico para municГғВӯpios afetados pelo despovoamento, vilas e ГғВЎreas funcionais. SГғВЈo necessГғВЎrias ГғВЎreas funcionais e uma polГғВӯtica de emprego dotada de serviГғВ§os que atraiam as pessoas e que nГғВЈo as expulsem.

Precisamos de iniciativas para jovens agricultores para que tambГғВ©m possam menos Altri e mais projetos, com direito a ficar.

ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ JoГғВЈo Oliveira (The Left). ГўВҖВ“ Senhor Presidente, Senhor ComissГғВЎrio Fitto, o dia em que fazemos o debate sobre este relatГғВіrio, a propГғВіsito da importГғВўncia da polГғВӯtica de coesГғВЈo para as zonas rurais, ГғВ© precisamente o dia em que a ComissГғВЈo dos OrГғВ§amentos acaba de votar alteraГғВ§ГғВөes aos regulamentos dos fundos europeus da polГғВӯtica de coesГғВЈo, nomeadamente o FEDER e o Fundo de CoesГғВЈo, que passam a ter como objetivos especГғВӯficos o militarismo.

A mobilidade militar na UniГғВЈo passou a ser um dos objetivos de utilizaГғВ§ГғВЈo dos fundos de coesГғВЈo.

E nГғВіs perguntamos: como ГғВ© que a mobilidade militar pode contribuir para o desenvolvimento das zonas rurais? O militarismo nГғВЈo serve a polГғВӯtica de coesГғВЈo, nem serve as zonas rurais e as suas necessidades especГғВӯficas, tal como nГғВЈo serve objetivos de polГғВӯticas setoriais que contrariam esta discussГғВЈo que estamos hoje aqui a ter.

Quando a UniГғВЈo Europeia financia o desenvolvimento da Rede Transeuropeia de Transportes, como estГғВЎ a fazer neste momento em Portugal, na ligaГғВ§ГғВЈo Sines-Caia, mas desconsidera a necessidade do investimento no aproveitamento da ligaГғВ§ГғВЈo ferroviГғВЎria para as populaГғВ§ГғВөes dessas regiГғВөes, nГғВЈo estГғВЎ a contribuir para a coesГғВЈo, nem para o desenvolvimento das zonas rurais. Estes sГғВЈo objetivos das polГғВӯticas setoriais que tГғВӘm de ser considerados tambГғВ©m.

ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ ГҺВӣГҺВөГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВӯГҸВҒГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВқГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВ¬ГҺВҝГҸВ…-ГҺВ‘ГҺВ»ГҺВұГҺВІГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВӮ (NI). ГўВҖВ“ ГҺВҡГҸВҚГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВө ГҺВ ГҸВҒГҸВҢГҺВөГҺВҙГҸВҒГҺВө, ГҺВҝГҺВ№ ГҺВІГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҺВәГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҸВҢГҸВҶГҺВҝГҺВ№ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВ•ГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҸВғГҺВұГҺВәГҺВҜГҺВ¶ГҺВҝГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҸВ…ГҺВҫГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВәГҸВҢГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВіГҸВүГҺВіГҺВ®ГҸВӮ, ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВөГҸВҶГҸВҢГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВұ, ГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВҚГҺВјГҺВұ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҺВӯГҺВ»ГҺВұГҺВ№ГҺВҝ, ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВјГҺВ·ГҺВҙГҺВұГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ¶ГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВјГҺВөГҺВіГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҶГҺВӯГҸВӮ, ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҺВјГҸВҚГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВјГҺВөГҸВғГҺВ¬ГҺВ¶ГҺВҝГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВұГҺВіГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҺВ¶ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҠГҸВҢГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҸВғГҺВө ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҸВҚ ГҸВҮГҺВұГҺВјГҺВ·ГҺВ»ГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВјГҺВӯГҸВӮ.

ГҺВ•ГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВ»ГҺВӯГҸВғГҺВјГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВјГҺВөГҺВіГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВұГҺВҜГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҺВіГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҸВӮ, ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҸВүГҺВөГҺВҪГҸВүГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВұГҺВәГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВҡГҺВ“ГҺВ  ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВӯГҸВҶГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВө ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҸВҮГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВіГҺВәГҸВҒГҺВөГҺВјГҺВҝГҸВҚ. ГҺВ‘ГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВ¬ ГҺВөГҸВ…ГҺВёГҸВҚГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҸВғГҺВәГҺВ¬ГҺВҪГҺВҙГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВҝ ГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҺВҙГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВҹГҺВ ГҺВ•ГҺВҡГҺВ•ГҺВ ГҺВ•, ГҺВјГҺВө ГҺВөГҸВ…ГҺВёГҸВҚГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҸВғГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҸВ…ГҺВІГҺВӯГҸВҒГҺВҪГҺВ·ГҸВғГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВқГҺВӯГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВ”ГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВҝГҺВәГҸВҒГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВҜГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВҝГҺВ·ГҺВіГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВјГҺВөГҺВҪГҸВүГҺВҪ. ГҺВ— ГҺВ•ГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҸВүГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҠГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВҲГҺВҪГҸВүГҸВғГҺВ· ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВҚГҸВғГҺВө ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВ® ГҸВғГҺВө ГҺВІГҺВ¬ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҸВҺГҺВҪ, ГҸВҮГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВ·ГҺВіГҸВҺГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВҮГҸВҚГҸВғГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВҙГҺВөГҺВјГҺВӯГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҸВҢ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВәГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҶГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҢ ГҺВәГҺВөГҸВҶГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВұГҺВ№ГҺВҝ, ГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВјГҺВҝГҺВҜГҸВҒГҺВұГҸВғГҺВјГҺВұ ГҺВөГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҺВҙГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВөГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҸВғГҺВө ГҺВјГҺВ· ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВӮ-ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҚГҸВҮГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ¬ ГҺВІГҺВҝГҸВғГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҸВҢГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҺВұ.

ГҺВ ГҸВҒГҺВӯГҸВҖГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВіГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҺВ¬ГҺВјГҺВөГҸВғГҺВұ ГҺВҝГҺВ№ ГҸВҖГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҸВүГҺВјГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВөГҺВәГҺВәГҸВҒГҺВөГҺВјГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВҜГҺВҫГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҸВғГҸВҚГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВұ ГҸВҺГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВөГҺВҫГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВёГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВҪ ГҺВҝГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВӮ. ГҺВҹГҺВ№ ГҺВІГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВҒГҸВҒГҺВҜГҸВҲГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВөГҸВ…ГҸВҒГҸВүГҺВөГҺВҪГҸВүГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВұГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВјГҺВјГҺВ® ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВҫГҺВөГҺВәГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВ¶ГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҺВәГҸВҢГҺВјГҺВјГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҸВҖГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВҒГҸВҢ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҸВҢГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВ¬ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҶГҺВұГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВҪ. ГҺВқГҺВұ ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВјГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВ…ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВҪ ГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВҡГҺВҡГҺВ• ГҸВҖГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВөГҸВҚГҺВҝГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВӮ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВҜГҺВ·ГҸВғГҺВ· ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВ¬ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ, ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВ¬ГҺВіГҺВәГҺВөГҸВӮ.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Vytenis Povilas Andriukaitis (S&D). ГўВҖВ“ Gerbiamas posГ„В—dГ…Вҫio pirmininke, dГ„В—koju praneГ…ВЎГ„В—jui. Tikrai puikus raportas ir, gerbiamas komisare, iГ…ВЎklausГ„В—t labai daug gerГ…Ві pasiГ…В«lymГ…Ві. Neabejotina, kad sanglaudos politikos srityje reikalingos horizontalios programos, kurios apimtГ…Ві Г…ВЎvietimo, sveikatos, skaitmeninГ„В—s infrastruktГ…В«ros kompleksiГ…ВЎkumГ„В…, ir nustatytos sГ„В…lygos (conditionality), kad niekas, net ir Г…ВЎalis narГ„В—, negalГ„В—tГ…Ві pakeisti, nes didieji miestai, didieji regionai ir parlamentuose, kur daug stipresnГ„В—s yra kitos jГ„В—gos, nuskriaudГ…Вҫia kaimo teritorijas. Kitas dalykas, pritraukti jaunimГ„В… galima tiktai investuojant stipriai Г„ВҜ paГ…Вҫangias Г…В«kininkavimo formas ГўВҖВ“ patrauklias, ГўВҖВһadvanced farmingГўВҖВң. Tos paГ…Вҫangios formos ГўВҖВ“ su robotizacija, su dirbtiniu intelektu, naudojant Г„ВҜvairias naujas technologijas ir naujas veisles ГўВҖВ“ ir augalГ…Ві, ir taip toliau. Tas patrauktГ…Ві jaunimГ„В…, nes jaunimas yra patrauklus mokslui ir gerai infrastruktГ…В«rai.

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ ГҺВ“ГҺВөГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВ“ГҺВөГҺВ¬ГҺВҙГҺВ· (ECR). ГўВҖВ“ ГҺВҡГҸВҚГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВө ГҺВ ГҸВҒГҸВҢГҺВөГҺВҙГҸВҒГҺВө, ГҸВ„ГҸВҢГҸВғГҺВҝ ГҸВүГҸВӮ ECR ГҸВҢГҸВғГҺВҝ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВүГҸВӮ ГҺВ•ГҺВёГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҢ ГҺВӣГҺВұГҸВҠГҺВәГҸВҢ ГҺВңГҺВӯГҸВ„ГҸВүГҸВҖГҺВҝ ГҺВҙГҺВҜГҺВҪГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВјГҺВө ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВөГҺВҪГҺВҜГҸВғГҸВҮГҸВ…ГҸВғГҺВ· ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҺГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҸВҺГҺВҪ ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҮГҸВҺГҺВҪ. ГҺВ“ГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВөГҺВјГҺВ¬ГҸВӮ, ГҺВ· ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВұГҸВғГҸВҶГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВ· ГҺВөГҺВҪГҸВҢГҸВӮ ГҺВІГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВјГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВјГҺВӯГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВӮ ГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҮГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГўВҖВ”ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҺВәГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҺВҙГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВҚГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҺВ»ГҸВҢГҺВіГҸВү ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВіГҺВ®ГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВҪГҸВғГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ… ГҸВҖГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҺВёГҸВ…ГҸВғГҺВјГҺВҝГҸВҚ, ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҸВ…ГҸВҶГҺВ№ГҺВ»ГҺВҜГҺВұГҸВӮ, ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВөГҺВіГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВҲГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҺВҪГҺВӯГҸВүГҺВҪ, ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВӯГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВ№ГҸВҲГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВғГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВғГҺВјГҺВӯГҺВҪГҸВүГҺВҪ ГҺВөГҸВ…ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВҺГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВғГҸВҮГҸВҢГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВғГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВ№ГҺВҪГҸВүГҺВҪГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВӯГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВҫГҺВ·ГҸВӮГўВҖВ” ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВәГҺВҝГҸВҒГҸВүГҺВҪГҺВҜГҺВҙГҺВұ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВјГҺВұГҸВӮ.

ГҺВ‘ГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВҜГҺВ»ГҺВөГҺВәГҸВ„ГҺВұ, ГҺВҝГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҮГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВҚГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВ»ГҺВҜГҺВәГҺВҪГҺВҝ ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВұГҺВіГҸВүГҺВіГҺВ®ГҸВӮ ГҺВіГҺВөГҸВүГҸВҒГҺВіГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҺГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВұГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҶГҺВ№ГҺВәГҸВҺГҺВҪ ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҠГҸВҢГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҸВүГҺВҪ, ГҺВөГҺВҪГҸВҺ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҺВ»ГҺВұ ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВұГҸВҶГҸВ…ГҺВ»ГҺВ¬ГҸВғГҸВғГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВұГҺВҪГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВ¬ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВәГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВ¬. ГҺВ“ГҺВ№ГҺВұ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВөГҺВҫГҺВұГҸВғГҸВҶГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВ· ГҺВјГҺВұГҺВәГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҖГҸВҒГҸВҢГҺВёГҺВөГҸВғГҺВјГҺВ· ГҺВІГҺВ№ГҸВүГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВјГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВ¬ ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ, ГҺВҝГҺВ№ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҸВҮГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВӯГҸВҖГҺВөГҺВ№ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВұГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВәГҸВ„ГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВјГҺВ· ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҸВҢГҸВғГҺВІГҺВұГҸВғГҺВ· ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҸВ…ГҺВіГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҸВҖГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВёГҺВұГҺВ»ГҸВҲГҺВ·, ГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВҪГҺВҙГҺВөГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВјГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВұ, ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҸВҖГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВғГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҺВ® ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВӯГҺВіГҺВұГҸВғГҺВ·, ГҸВ„ГҺВҝ ГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВҒГҸВҢ, ГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВөГҺВәГҸВҖГҺВұГҺВҜГҺВҙГҺВөГҸВ…ГҸВғГҺВ·, ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВ·ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҺВҝГҺВҙГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҺВ¬ГҺВ»ГҺВ»ГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҺВІГҺВұГҸВғГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҸВ…ГҸВҖГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВөГҸВғГҺВҜГҺВөГҸВӮ.

ГҺВ— ГҺВ•ГҸВҖГҺВ№ГҸВ„ГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВҖГҺВ® ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВұ ГҺВәГҸВҒГҺВ¬ГҸВ„ГҺВ· ГҺВјГҺВӯГҺВ»ГҺВ· ГҺВӯГҸВҮГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВёГҺВ®ГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВҪ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВӯГҸВҮГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҺВөГҸВҖГҺВұГҸВҒГҺВәГҺВ® ГҸВҮГҸВҒГҺВ·ГҺВјГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҺВҙГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВғГҺВ·, ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВәГҺВұГҸВ„ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВ®ГҸВғГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ№ ГҺВҝГҸВҶГҺВөГҺВҜГҺВ»ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВҜГҺВҫГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҺВҪ ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВҝГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВіГҺВӯГҺВҪГҺВөГҺВ№ГҺВөГҸВӮ ГҸВҺГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВө ГҺВҪГҺВұ ГҺВҙГҺВ№ГҺВұГҸВғГҸВҶГҺВұГҺВ»ГҺВ№ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВөГҺВҜ ГҺВ· ГҺВөГҺВҪГҺВөГҸВҒГҺВіГҸВҢГҸВӮ ГҸВғГҸВ…ГҺВјГҺВјГҺВөГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВҮГҺВ® ГҸВ„ГҺВҝГҸВ…ГҸВӮ ГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҺВҪ ГҺВұГҺВіГҸВҒГҺВҝГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВ® ГҺВұГҺВҪГҺВ¬ГҸВҖГҸВ„ГҸВ…ГҺВҫГҺВ· ГҺВәГҺВұГҺВ№ ГҸВ„ГҺВ№ГҸВӮ ГҺВҝГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВҝГҺВҪГҺВҝГҺВјГҺВ№ГҺВәГҺВӯГҸВӮ ГҺВҙГҸВҒГҺВұГҸВғГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВҒГҺВ№ГҸВҢГҸВ„ГҺВ·ГҸВ„ГҺВөГҸВӮ.

ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Diana Iovanovici Г…ВһoГ…ВҹoacГ„Вғ (NI). ГўВҖВ“ Domnule preГҲВҷedinte, vorbeaГҲВӣi de faptul cГ„Вғ cetГ„ВғГҲВӣenii trebuie sГ„Вғ aibГ„Вғ ГҲВҷansa de a rГ„ВғmГғВўne ГғВ®n locurile ГғВ®n care s-au nГ„Вғscut. RomГғВўnii nu au avut aceastГ„Вғ ГҲВҷansГ„Вғ.

10 milioane de romГғВўni, jumГ„Вғtate din populaГҲВӣia RomГғВўniei, este nomadГ„Вғ ГғВ®n acest moment, ГғВ®n sensul ГғВ®n care a fost datГ„Вғ afarГ„Вғ din ГҲВӣarГ„Вғ de mГ„Вғsurile Uniunii Europene: pentru cГ„Вғ aГҲВӣi ГғВ®nchis mineritul, pГ„Вғdurile au fost luate de austrieci, iar la ГҲВӣarГ„Вғ nu au mai rГ„Вғmas decГғВўt oamenii bГ„ВғtrГғВўni. RomГғВўnii vГ„Вғ dezvoltГ„Вғ dumneavoastrГ„Вғ economiile, pentru cГ„Вғ nouГ„Вғ ne-aГҲВӣi ГғВ®nchis orice posibilitate de a ne dezvolta.

ГҲВҳtiГҲВӣi cГ„Вғ s-au desfiinГҲВӣat ГҲВҷcoli la ГҲВӣarГ„Вғ? ГҲВҳtiГҲВӣi cГ„Вғ nu mai sunt dispensare? ГҲВҳtiГҲВӣi cГ„Вғ acuma, tot venind de la Uniunea EuropeanГ„Вғ, li se interzice sГ„Вғ se mai ГғВ®ncГ„ВғlzeascГ„Вғ cu lemne? ГҲВҳtiГҲВӣi cГ„Вғ deГҲВҷi avem o treime din reГҲВӣeaua hidrograficГ„Вғ a Europei, romГғВўnilor le este interzis sГ„Вғ mai scoatГ„Вғ apГ„Вғ din fГғВўntГғВўnГ„Вғ sГ„Вғ-ГҲВҷi ude plantele? ГҲВҳtiГҲВӣi cГ„Вғ dumneavoastrГ„Вғ impuneГҲВӣi sГ„Вғ avem boli la animale, astfel ГғВ®ncГғВўt sГ„Вғ nu mai avem agriculturГ„Вғ ГҲВҷi zootehnie?

ГӮВ 
ГӮВ ГӮВ 
ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Juan Fernando LГғВіpez Aguilar (S&D). ГўВҖВ“ SeГғВұor presidente, seГғВұor vicepresidente Fitto, seguramente no le extraГғВұa que desde la bancada socialista subrayemos siempre que la polГғВӯtica de cohesiГғВіn es la razГғВіn de ser de Europa: solidaridad regional, pero tambiГғВ©n social. Y no le extraГғВұarГғВЎ tampoco que ponga el acento en la dimensiГғВіn de la polГғВӯtica regional en las regiones rurales ГўВҖВ”tambiГғВ©n en las regiones ultraperifГғВ©ricasГўВҖВ”, porque simplificar significa reducir cargas burocrГғВЎticas y administrativas, pero no los objetivos de la propia polГғВӯtica de cohesiГғВіn.

Y creo que es muy importante que, cuando el Parlamento ha apostado por un incremento de los fondos especГғВӯficos para apoyar a las regiones rurales y las producciones rurales en regiones ultraperifГғВ©ricas ГўВҖВ”los fondosГӮВ POSEIГўВҖВ”, las regiones ultraperifГғВ©ricas sepan que van a tener su asiento en el rediseГғВұo de la polГғВӯtica de cohesiГғВіn en las regiones rurales para que puedan comercializar sus productos estratГғВ©gicos de una forma justa.

ГӮВ 

ГӮВ ГӮВ Raffaele Fitto, Executive Vice-President of the Commission. ГўВҖВ“ Mr President, thank you for your contribution, of which I have taken good note. I appreciate your insights on the challenges the rural areas face and the significant role that cohesion policy plays in shaping the future of the EU's rural areas.

You rightly point out the development of infrastructure, particularly in the fields of transport, energy and digital connectivity, alongside essential services for improving the quality of life in rural areas. The reduction of economic, social and territorial disparities will continue to remain at the core of cohesion policy, providing critical support to rural areas.

Your report and interventions today reaffirm this importance and will further guide our discussions and our work for the future of rural areas.

I would like to give only two messages.

First, many problems that you mentioned are the priority of the mid-term review, like water, housing, energy and competitiveness. And I remember to all of you that mid-term review is a voluntary basis. So defence is a possibility. And in particular for eastern border regions that have to face not only the challenge regarding defence but also the new economic challenges.

Second message, we can work together using also the new governance of the European Commission. As you know, under my executive vice-presidency we have a coordination of three commissioners: agriculture, tourism and transport, fisheries and blue economy. And I agreed with the three commissioners that we must work with a common vision to prepare the strategy for internal rural areas, starting by this important and very positive report.
